#METABOLOMICS WORKBENCH STUDY_ID:ST000121 ANALYSIS_ID:AN000203
VERSION             	1
CREATED_ON          	2016-09-17
#PROJECT
PR:PROJECT_TITLE                 	Impact of anesthesia and euthanasia on metabolomics of mammalian tissues:
PR:PROJECT_TITLE                 	in a C57BL/6J mouse model
PR:PROJECT_TYPE                  	Anesthesia effect study
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	We examined, for the first time using untargeted and targeted metabolomics, the
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	of several commonly-used methods of anesthesia and euthanasia for collection of
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	muscle, liver, heart, adipose and serum of C57BL/6J mice. The data revealed
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	impacts of different anesthesia and euthanasia strategies. Based on these
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	we present a more optimal collection strategy mammalian tissues and recommend
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	rodent tissues intended for metabolomics studies be collected under anesthesia
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	than post-euthanasia.
PR:INSTITUTE                     	University of Michigan
PR:DEPARTMENT                    	Internal Medicine
PR:LABORATORY                    	Evans lab / Burant lab
PR:LAST_NAME                     	Evans
PR:FIRST_NAME                    	Charles
PR:ADDRESS                       	6321 Brehm Tower, 1000 Wall St.
PR:EMAIL                         	chevans@umich.edu
PR:PHONE                         	734-232-8177
PR:FUNDING_SOURCE                	National Institute of Diabetes and Digestive and Kidney Diseases (NIDDK),
PR:FUNDING_SOURCE                	Institutes of Health
#STUDY
ST:STUDY_TITLE                   	Impact of anesthesia and euthanasia on metabolomics of mammalian tissues:
ST:STUDY_TITLE                   	in a C57BL/6J mouse model
ST:STUDY_TYPE                    	Anesthesia effect study
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	We examined the effect of several commonly-used methods of anesthesia and
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	for collection of skeletal muscle, liver, heart, adipose and serum of C57BL/6J
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	The data revealed tissue-specific impacts of different anesthesia and
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	strategies. Based on these findings, we present a more optimal collection
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	mammalian tissues and recommend that rodent tissues intended for metabolomics
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	be collected under anesthesia rather than post-euthanasia.
ST:INSTITUTE                     	University of Michigan
ST:DEPARTMENT                    	Internal Medicine
ST:LABORATORY                    	Evans Lab / Burant Lab
ST:LAST_NAME                     	Charles
ST:FIRST_NAME                    	Evans
ST:ADDRESS                       	6321 Brehm Tower, 1000 Wall Street, Ann Arbor MI 48105
ST:EMAIL                         	chevans@umich.edu
ST:PHONE                         	734-232-8177
ST:NUM_GROUPS                    	6
ST:TOTAL_SUBJECTS                	49

#COLLECTION
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	4 tissues plus blood serum were collected and immediately following euthanasia
CO:COLLECTION_SUMMARY            	anesthesia induction, frozen in liquid nitrogen and stored at -80C until
CO:SAMPLE_TYPE                   	Skeletal muscle (gastrocnemius), Liver, Heart, Epididymal white adipose (fat),
CO:SAMPLE_TYPE                   	serum
CO:COLLECTION_METHOD             	Surgical dissection
CO:COLLECTION_TIME               	As soon as possible following anesthesia/euthanasia (all tissues collected
CO:COLLECTION_TIME               	3 minutes)
CO:STORAGE_CONDITIONS            	-80 C
#TREATMENT
TR:TREATMENT_SUMMARY             	Mice were prepared or tissue collection by one of 6 modes of anesthesia or
TR:TREATMENT_SUMMARY             	then tissues were rapidly surgically collected and frozen
TR:ANIMAL_ANESTHESIA             	One of 6 methods: 1) Cervical dislocation, 2) Carbon dioxide inhalation, 3)
TR:ANIMAL_ANESTHESIA             	overdose, 4) continuous isoflurane, 5) ketamine, 6) pentobarbital
TR:ANIMAL_FASTING                	5 hours
TR:ANIMAL_ENDP_EUTHANASIA        	All tissue collection were terminal studies; in methods 1-3, animals were
TR:ANIMAL_ENDP_EUTHANASIA        	prior to tissue collection; in methods 4-6, animals were under deep anesthesia
TR:ANIMAL_ENDP_EUTHANASIA        	tissues were collected.
#SAMPLEPREP
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	Frozen tissue samples were pulverized in a liquid nitrogen-chilled mortar and
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	then sonicated in cold extraction solvent (7:2:1 methanol:chloroform:water) at
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	approximate ratio of 30 mg tissue (wet mass) /1 mL of solvent. After allowing
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	to rest on ice 5 minutes, they were centrifuged to pellet precipitated protein
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	cell debris; the supernatant was placed in autosampler vials for direct LC-MS
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	For serum, extraction solvent (1:1:1 methanol:acetonitrile:acetone) was added
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	serum at a 4:1 solvent:serum ratio, vortexed to mix, then centrifuged and
SP:SAMPLEPREP_SUMMARY            	recovered for LC-MS analysis.
SP:SAMPLEPREP_PROTOCOL_FILENAME  	PROTOCOLS_mouse_anesthesia.pdf
SP:PROCESSING_METHOD             	Cryo-pulverization + sonication in extraction solvent
#CHROMATOGRAPHY
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_SUMMARY        	Polar metabolites were analyzed by HILIC-MS using an aminopropyl stationary
CH:CHROMATOGRAPHY_TYPE           	-
CH:INSTRUMENT_NAME               	Agilent 1200
CH:COLUMN_NAME                   	Phenonmenex Luna NH2 3u, 150 mm x 2.1 mm ID
CH:COLUMN_PRESSURE               	150 bar
CH:COLUMN_TEMPERATURE            	25 C
CH:FLOW_GRADIENT                 	80-0% B over 20 minutes, hold 4 minutes, return to 80%B
CH:FLOW_RATE                     	0.25 mL/min
CH:SAMPLE_INJECTION              	25 uL
CH:SOLVENT_A                     	5 mM ammonium acetate in water, adjusted to pH 9.9 using ammonium hydroxide
CH:SOLVENT_B                     	Acetonitrile
CH:ANALYTICAL_TIME               	32 min
